  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8e8eee54-5c41-4087-8d3c-ecd8cf8eaaf4'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText1648592338247080796" style="display:none">Aerial combat brings a thrilling new dimension to the Napoleonic Wars as valiant warriors ride mighty fighting dragons, bred for size or speed. When HMS Reliant captures a French frigate and seizes the precious cargo, an unhatched dragon egg, fate sweeps Captain Will Laurence from his seafaring life into an uncertain future – and an unexpected kinship with a most extraordinary creature. Thrust into the rarified world of the Aerial Corps as master of the dragon Temeraire, he will face a crash course in the daring tactics of airborne battle. For as France’s own dragon-borne forces rally to breach British soil in Bonaparte’s boldest gambit, Laurence and Temeraire must soar into their own baptism of fire.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There's one small romance, but it's very short, ungraphic, and irrelevant to the overall plot. Seems almost like it was just kind of thrown in there b<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There's one small romance, but it's very short, ungraphic, and irrelevant to the overall plot. Seems almost like it was just kind of thrown in there because she thought it needed one. But I found it refreshing to read a book who's driving force wasn't romance for once.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

I read Uprooted first and loved<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The books aren't related in any way, so you can read either one first, depending upon what you're in the mood to read. I read Uprooted first and loved it, and now I'm starting in on this series which has a completely different feel, but seems well written, too. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_2796676" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2796676" />
    <a title="Dafna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/163946-dafna"><img alt="Dafna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1184150899p2/163946.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2796676?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dafna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dafna" href="/user/show/163946-dafna">Dafna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2796676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer619470776422672987">God, I admit, I'm one of those douchey fucks that look down on fantasy readers while I sit firmly ensconced in my igloo composed of "Star Wars: Rogue Squadron" and "Star Trek: The Lost Years" books. Of course, it'd be a book about dragons fighting for the British army against the encroaching Napoleonic forces to get to me to realize: DRAGONS ARE FUCKING COOL.<br/><br/>Especially dragons with awesome Han Solo type female riders and plucky young girls manning the gunnery and uptight, strong silent type men </span>
  <span id="freeText619470776422672987" style="display:none">God, I admit, I'm one of those douchey fucks that look down on fantasy readers while I sit firmly ensconced in my igloo composed of "Star Wars: Rogue Squadron" and "Star Trek: The Lost Years" books. Of course, it'd be a book about dragons fighting for the British army against the encroaching Napoleonic forces to get to me to realize: DRAGONS ARE FUCKING COOL.<br /><br />Especially dragons with awesome Han Solo type female riders and plucky young girls manning the gunnery and uptight, strong silent type men of good standing learning to fight dirty. I <i>love</i> this shit, guys.<br /><br />I don't know, I'll probably turn into a furry soon, but until then I'll be curled up under my comforter, the next book tucked under my pillow as I periodically wake myself in the middle of the night by shouting "FLY, BITCHES, FLY."<br /><br />Sorry Han Yee.</span>
  <a data-text-id="619470776422672987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_615142614" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/615142614" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/615142614?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18626894-his-majesty-s-dragon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=that-bastard">that-bastard</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=i-cried">i-cried</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=audible">audible</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer615142614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17952278155378364139"><b>2/7/18 - ON SALE for $2.99:</b> <br/><br/><a href='https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B000GCFBQA/ref=as_li_ss_il?caller=Goodreads&callerLink=https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18626894-his-majesty-s-dragon&linkCode=li1&tag=rabrea-20&linkId=f79fa5c05975881526d447106c2e149d' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457957263i/18425626.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506790036i/24053202.gif' width='1' height='1' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://amzn.to/2xJIt5C'>http://amzn.to/2xJIt5C</a><br/><br/><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2015/03/review-his-majestys-dragon-by-naomi-novik.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>This isn't my first Novik read. In fact, the whole reason I finally got on with reading HIS MAJESTY'S DRAGON is b/c I read and absolutely adored <b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764-uprooted' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Uprooted</a>
</b>. But UPROOTED isn't being released until May, so this is the first Novik review I've posted.<br/><br/>Same and <em>not</em> the same, people. Same and <em>not</em> the same.<br/><br/>Meet Will Laurence:<br/><br/>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423406015i/13620642.jpg' width='400' height='167' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
<br/><br/>Laurence is a Captain in the British Navy. He is a perfect gentlemen. He is ostentatiously dull.</span>
  <span id="freeText17952278155378364139" style="display:none"><b>2/7/18 - ON SALE for $2.99:</b> <br><br><a href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B000GCFBQA/ref=as_li_ss_il?caller=Goodreads&amp;callerLink=https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18626894-his-majesty-s-dragon&amp;linkCode=li1&amp;tag=rabrea-20&amp;linkId=f79fa5c05975881526d447106c2e149d" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457957263i/18425626.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506790036i/24053202.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/2xJIt5C">http://amzn.to/2xJIt5C</a><br><br><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2015/03/review-his-majestys-dragon-by-naomi-novik.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>This isn't my first Novik read. In fact, the whole reason I finally got on with reading HIS MAJESTY'S DRAGON is b/c I read and absolutely adored <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764-uprooted" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Uprooted</a>
</b>. But UPROOTED isn't being released until May, so this is the first Novik review I've posted.<br><br>Same and <em>not</em> the same, people. Same and <em>not</em> the same.<br><br>Meet Will Laurence:<br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423406015i/13620642.jpg" width="400" height="167" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>Laurence is a Captain in the British Navy. He is a perfect gentlemen. He is ostentatiously dull. <br><br>And while there is significant character growth throughout the book, it is completely in regards to the small-mindedness that comes with his gentleman status, having no impact whatsoever on the dull, dull, dullness of his disposition. <br><br>And maybe this is irrelevant, and maybe it isn't. I don't know. What I <em>do</em> know is that b/c I have <b>
  <a href="http://www.imdb.com/character/ch0001246" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">James Norrington</a>
</b> in my head, every time Laurence is on the page--and that's pretty much all the time--all I can think is: <br><br>Why on earth would you write a Norrington-like character, when you could write a <b>
  <a href="http://www.imdb.com/character/ch0001220" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Will Turner</a>
</b>:<br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423406228i/13620689.jpg" width="236" height="354" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>or <b>
  <a href="http://www.imdb.com/character/ch0001274" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Jack Sparrow</a>
</b>:<br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423406303i/13620695.jpg" width="445" height="297" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>type character instead? <br><br>Especially, when the Norrington-type character has a DRAGON? B/c <em>really</em>? What would Norrington do with a dragon?<br><br>Funnily enough, I now feel qualified to answer that question: not much.<br><br>That's not to say it didn't have its moments. Obviously, it did. B/c dragon. <br><br>Temeraire was probably my favorite part of the book. BUT. I couldn’t completely enjoy his character, b/c Novik states early on that Chinese dragons are bred for intelligence, and after establishing that fact, uses him to spout insightful and ahead-of-his-time political ideals. BUT. For an "insightful" character to be perceived as insightful (for me, anyway), he needs to be spouting universal truths, timeless wisdoms, or exposing easily overlooked, but once pointed out, clear flaws in a majority mindset. <br><br>All Temeraire does is say things like:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Some of the laws which I have heard make very little sense, and I do not know that I would obey them if it were not to oblige you. It seems to me that if you wish to apply laws to us, it were only reasonable to consult us on them, and from what you have read to me about Parliament, I do not think any dragons are invited to go there."</i>
</blockquote><br>Which, <em>yes</em>, is amusing, but not particularly clever. <br><br>I also enjoyed Laurence’s pragmatic observations, which were quietly humorous and made me snicker at regular intervals. Like when it’s discovered that the dragon egg they acquired will hatch before reaching land and one of the crew will have to bond with the hatchling, meaning that he'll be forced to leave the respectable Navy to join the disreputable Dragon Aviators. <br><br>Laurence is determined—as any gentleman would be—to proceed in all fairness:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>. . . though if Fanshawe had not spoken in so unbecoming a way, Laurence would have liked to keep Carver out of it, as he knew the boy had a poor head for heights, which struck him as a grave impediment for an aviator.</i>
</blockquote><br>*snickers*<br><br>But regular though those intervals were, they were not enough to overwhelm the blah. <br><br>Most of the blah was the result of Laurence's stodginess, but while it's one thing to accurately reflect the attitudes of the period in which a book is set, it's quite another to tacitly endorse them:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<i>"Laurence bowed to them both, though he had a sense of awkwardness for the first occasion since he had grown used to Harcourt. She was leaning with no appearance of consciousness against Choiseul's shoulder, and he was looking down at her with undisguised warmth; she was quite young, after all, and Laurence could not help feeling the absence of any suitable chaperone."</i><br><br>She was young. And in need. Of a chaperone. <br><br>*flares nostrils*<br><br>The suggestion is bad enough, but when Harcourt was indeed taken advantage of by the dastardly Choiseul, thus justifying Laurence's backward thinking . . . *frowns*  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br> <br>I also found it difficult to believe that a man so distraught over the inability to pursue elements essential to his own happiness--like a wife, children, and a quiet life in the country--after becoming saddled with a dragon, could transition into his new life so completely, even going so far as to compare overzealously praising Temeraire to the exasperating drivel spewed from men too enamored of their own relations:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>With difficulty he restrained himself from boasting further; nothing, he was sure, could be more irritating, like one of those men who could not stop talking of the beauty of their mistress, or the cleverness of their children.</i>
</blockquote><br>Then there were the inconsistencies. Like how Temeraire's egg managed to survive aboard a cold, damp boat for a month or more and afterwards being told that the dragon eggs are kept in the hottest part of the training facility's Roman baths, b/c the female dragons have neither the time nor inclination to sit on them until they hatch, and they can't be buried in the hot ash at the base of a volcano, b/c no volcanoes.<br><br>*sighs*<br><br>I heard a sermon once where the pastor quoted something about the saints crying out, "How long?" in reference to church-services-that-never-end and it was both shocking and hilarious enough to stick with me.<br><br>And when I found myself crying out, “How long?” several times while reading HIS MAJESTY'S DRAGON, I was surprised b/c it’s not a particularly lengthy book.<br><br>But by golly, it felt like it was.<br><br>SO. If you like novels of manners, the Napoleonic Wars, and dragons, then by all means, read this book. I am a lone quantity. Everyone else seems to LOVE HIS MAJESTY'S DRAGON, it won all kinds of awards, and even I will admit that it is incredibly well written. Novik is a superb method writer, if there is such a thing. HOWEVER . . . if you <em>aren't</em> crazy about the idea of a gentlemanly account of said war, but think it <em>might</em> be okay b/c DRAGONS . . . I strongly suggest that you are mistaken. Recommended with qualifications.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17952278155378364139" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText10127522607494620681" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read with my wonderful friend, Ashley *Hufflepuff Kitten* =)</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488068961i/22078108._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>****I reckon' I'm going to be <b>spoilery!</b>****<br><br>Once again I'm going to say, "Why did it take me so long to read this?" I want one too dang it. ❤<br><br>Laurence was a captain on a Naval ship when they found a French ship with an egg on it. Well, of course they took the egg and when it hatched, the little black dragon picked Laurence. Well, life as he knew it was over as he was going to have to leave the Navy and train with the Aerial Corps. They ride dragons and have a crew on the dragon with you and fight the enemy. Oh what joy! <br><br>I loved all of the dragons in the book and there were several of the men and women I loved too. For the love of all that's holy, I want a talking dragon! I wish my dog could talk too but then they both would probably drive me crazy, but I digress! <br><br>Anyway, most of the book is about training Laurence and Temeraire with the other dragons and captains but it was so much fun. There are a few battles they get into a little later but setting up this world was so freaking awesome. I have never had so much fun. I mean talking dragons, how could you not love it. The camaraderie between the humans, dragons and other humans were amaze balls. <br><br>This book has went on my favorites list and I sooooooo look forward to the rest of the books!<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/02/his-majestys-dragon-by-naomi-novik.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<div id="review_2909141" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2909141" />
    <a title="Irene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/181728-irene"><img alt="Irene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1184116724p2/181728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2909141?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irene" href="/user/show/181728-irene">Irene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2909141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12706956549704053032">I wasn't expecting much when I picked up <i>His Majesty's Dragon.</i> To tell the truth, if I'd seen it in a bookstore, I wouldn't have picked it up. But it was recommended to me by a reliable source as a better alternative to Eragon, and it was a historical fantasy set during the Napoleonic Wars. I figured I'd give it a try. I didn't regret it.<br/><br/>I don't love this book because Naomi Novik's writing style is equal to that of Tolkien. I don't love this book because it's perfect in every way - indeed, some </span>
  <span id="freeText12706956549704053032" style="display:none">I wasn't expecting much when I picked up <i>His Majesty's Dragon.</i> To tell the truth, if I'd seen it in a bookstore, I wouldn't have picked it up. But it was recommended to me by a reliable source as a better alternative to Eragon, and it was a historical fantasy set during the Napoleonic Wars. I figured I'd give it a try. I didn't regret it.<br /><br />I don't love this book because Naomi Novik's writing style is equal to that of Tolkien. I don't love this book because it's perfect in every way - indeed, some of the subplots were rather weak, and should have been changed or cut out altogether. Rather, I love this book because Naomi Novik took a boring, cliche idea, and put on a spin on it that's so brilliant and yet mind-bogglingly obvious I have to wonder why in the world someone hadn't thought of it before.<br /><br />In all of the previous dragonrider books I'd read, there was always one rider. One lone human on a dragon the size of a house. And somehow, that was supposed to be special and sensible and realistic. But no - if a dragon is that large, then why is there only one rider? Why can't there be more? Having one rider on a dragon is like putting one passenger on a plane that could potentially carry fifty.<br /><br />And that's where Naomi Novik takes the Temeraire series. Her fight scenes aren't one-on-one affairs, they're all-out aerial battles fought with crew members dangling precariously from leather harnesses, forced to make the best of inaccurate rifles. It's true, the captain has a special relationship with his or her dragon, but there's the distinct feeling of a team - that the captain would really be nowhere without the support of a crew behind him. What's more, Novik makes the battles <i>work</i> - they're clearly planned out and make sense in a historical context.<br /><br />The main characters are also unusually engaging - Laurence, as a former naval captain who accidentally stumbles upon a dragon egg, is plunged into a branch of the military completely unlike the one in which he's served, and his confusion and stiffness are only to be expected. While his stubbornness and sense of propriety are on occasion mildly irritating, his reactions to elements of the Aerial Corps are only natural given his character. And Temeraire, the dragon that hatches from the egg Laurence discovers, is more than a mere sentient ship - his naive, inquisitive personality is adorably appealing, and the political views he develops at times contrast sharply with those of Laurence.<br /><br />And then there's the matter of the main villain - there is none. There's no evil overlord to face, no Dark Lord Napoleon who tries to foil Laurence's and Temeraire's plans at every turn. In fact, despite the fact that the book is from a strictly British point of view, Novik portrays Napoleon fairly, and his character only grows more sympathetic as the series goes on. Napoleon doesn't even make an appearance during the first book - it's just the British Aerial Corps versus the French Armee de l'Air. It's a lovely change; as the battles grow steadily more climactic, one gets the feeling that they're in a war against other dragon-crews just like theirs, not fighting some unseen maniac.<br /><br />Like I said, <i>His Majesty's Dragon</i> isn't perfect. The subplot with Choiseul is ultimately disappointing in its resolution, and Laurence's love interest is perilously close to a Mary-Sue and should have been cut (thankfully, there's a lot less of her in the following books). Still, it's a refreshingly original spin on an overused idea, and all in all a very good read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12706956549704053032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2051848856" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2051848856" />
    <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller"><img alt="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517553177p2/13396599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2051848856?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller">Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2051848856" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1721744390266616583">[4.5/5 stars] <i>Woe is me</i> for not having read this years ago!<br/><br/>I had this amazing dragon book sitting unread on my shelf for over 10 years… and I’m surprised no one revoked my membership to the dragon obsession club (not a real thing). In all fairness, the way people described this book and series gave me a very different impression than what the first book actually entailed. They’d say, “it’s an alternate military history, but with dragons.” I’m sure that description is completely accurate for the </span>
  <span id="freeText1721744390266616583" style="display:none">[4.5/5 stars] <i>Woe is me</i> for not having read this years ago!<br><br>I had this amazing dragon book sitting unread on my shelf for over 10 years… and I’m surprised no one revoked my membership to the dragon obsession club (not a real thing). In all fairness, the way people described this book and series gave me a very different impression than what the first book actually entailed. They’d say, “it’s an alternate military history, but with dragons.” I’m sure that description is completely accurate for the series as a whole, but had someone mentioned even briefly that His Majesty’s Dragon was less about alt-history as a focus (even though that was an essential setting component) and more about the forming bond between a man and his dragon, I’d have been on board the Temeraire ship years ago. Unfortunately first impressions caused me to hold off. When it came out I was in the middle of college and the last thing I wanted to do was put down one text book and pick up another (even if the new one had dragons). I thought I’d be bored with the historical elements and recycled battle scenes. All the discussions I’d had about it with customers made me think I was getting into a dry historical retelling that took itself too seriously. This is SO NOT THE CASE!!<br><br>The relationship between man and dragon is 100% the appeal of the book for me. It’s a slowly paced plot that focuses on the bond and establishes the groundwork for what’s to come. Because of the aforementioned expectations for the series, I’m certain some ventured in looking for battle sequences, military strategy, and loads of historical references, but were bored with their lack (which is an irony considering my boredom might have stemmed from those things being present if I’d read it 10 years ago). As I said, perhaps the series as a whole will offer those things, but for me this book offered perfect immersion into what it’s like to be a dragonrider (or Aerialist) in training. <br><br>Now that my tastes have broadened, I’m actually looking forward to seeing the historical immersion in future books, but that alone wouldn’t have been enough to get me to pick up the series. The dragons are my main motivation. Not only was Temeraire a fascinating creature, but so were the many other varieties of dragons (aka Niki’s dragon heaven). I loved the training aspects and can’t wait to see those put into good use, I loved the commander of the training encampment (you’ll see), and I loved the relationships and dynamics beginning to form between all the trainees and their dragons. Basically, this is the book I’ve been hounding to find all my life. 😭<br><br>The slow burn of this novel might have bored a few people, but I reveled in every single moment. It had me so wrapped up, I even shed a tear or two (I can’t remember the last time a book made me cry). The combination of a fantastic main character, sentient dragons (filled with awesomeness), and the overall theme of the series set His Majesty’s Dragon up as one of the best books I’ve read in a while. I can’t wait to get my hands on the next one!<br><br><b>Recommendations:</b> Read this book if you like dragons. It’s a bonus if you also like alt-history. ;P<br><br>Via The Obsessive Bookseller at <a href="http://www.nikihawkes.com" rel="nofollow noopener">www.NikiHawkes.com </a> <br><br>Other books you might like:<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12974372.A_Natural_History_of_Dragons__The_Memoirs_of_Lady_Trent___1_" title="A Natural History of Dragons (The Memoirs of Lady Trent, #1) by Marie Brennan" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1359770409s/12974372.jpg" alt="A Natural History of Dragons (The Memoirs of Lady Trent, #1) by Marie Brennan" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/498139.Dragon_Weather__Obsidian_Chronicles___1_" title="Dragon Weather (Obsidian Chronicles, #1) by Lawrence Watt-Evans" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1312045392s/498139.jpg" alt="Dragon Weather (Obsidian Chronicles, #1) by Lawrence Watt-Evans" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13257637.The_Sweetest_Dark__The_Sweetest_Dark___1_" title="The Sweetest Dark (The Sweetest Dark, #1) by Shana Abe" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1335980437s/13257637.jpg" alt="The Sweetest Dark (The Sweetest Dark, #1) by Shana Abe" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17910124.The_Emperor_s_Blades__Chronicle_of_the_Unhewn_Throne___1_" title="The Emperor's Blades (Chronicle of the Unhewn Throne, #1) by Brian Staveley" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_1396564486" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1396564486" />
    <a title="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans"><img alt="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587115780p2/7298986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1396564486?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" href="/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans">✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18626894-his-majesty-s-dragon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=br-2015">br-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=absolute-favourites">absolute-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=military-deliciousness">military-deliciousness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1396564486" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer884257792681064333"><b>This book made me feel all warm and fuzzy inside</b>. Yes it did. Oh, I know exactly what you're thinking. You're thinking, "Sarah doesn't do warm and fuzzy, Sarah only does cold-hearted cynicism." Ha. Fooled you right there. <b>I'll have you know I do have a heart</b> (sometimes) and actually enjoy feeling all warm and fuzzy (occasionally). Besides, it's not like this is me cooing and getting the fuzzies over a bunch of cute babies. We're talking about dragons here, people!<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444666649i/16533378._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Wanna know why I'm all smitten a</b></span>
  <span id="freeText884257792681064333" style="display:none"><b>This book made me feel all warm and fuzzy inside</b>. Yes it did. Oh, I know exactly what you're thinking. You're thinking, "Sarah doesn't do warm and fuzzy, Sarah only does cold-hearted cynicism." Ha. Fooled you right there. <b>I'll have you know I do have a heart</b> (sometimes) and actually enjoy feeling all warm and fuzzy (occasionally). Besides, it's not like this is me cooing and getting the fuzzies over a bunch of cute babies. We're talking about dragons here, people!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444666649i/16533378._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Wanna know why I'm all smitten and stuff?</b> Mostly because this book reminded me of <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0076538/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pete's Dragon</a> <i>← I think I just lost half of the people reading this review. Don't worry kids, this is too ancient for you to know about. Besides, it's not your fault you were born two decades too late <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It does explain why you're all so screwed up, though <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.</i><br><br><b>So this is a story</b> about a <s>boy</s> man and his dragon. And this isn't typically the kind of book I enjoy reading because, let's be honest, there isn't much of a plot here. But the relationship between Laurence and his dragon Temeraire? It's everything. <b>It's cute beyond measure</b>. I know, I know, I just used the word cute *shudders* to describe the relationship between a grown man and a dragon. You can snicker all you want, I don't care. Because these two? <b>They make me all tingly inside</b>. Yes they do. I LOVE their conversations (yes, dragons do talk). I LOVE their interactions. I LOVE how much they care for each other. And I pretty much melt every time Laurence reads to Temeraire at night <i>← Damn. Either I'm getting really soft in my old age or Naomi Novik is a miracle worker.</i> Anyhow, <b>Laurence and Temeraire are so perfect for each other I think they should get married</b>. Or something.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444666981ra/16533404.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><b>Okay, I have to admit</b> Laurence could have been a bit more dashing. Strike that, he could have been a lot more dashing. But I still like him. He is nice, reliable, honourable and fair *shudders* <b>But I still like him</b>. I can't believe I'm actually admitting my utter fondness for a non-assholish male lead *gasps* Prepare to die everyone, the end of the world is near. <b>Chaos, doom and destruction await</b>.<br><br><b>Now for the other half of our perfect couple</b>: Temeraire. Sigh. I think I just fell in love with a dragon. I love his ever-innovative ideas about politics, his very fresh point of view and his <b>insightful comments</b>. His lines just crack me up. Besides, he loves being read French books on mathematics and physics, how can anyone resist that?! There are some very cool dragons in this book, but Temeraire here is <b>definitely my kind of monster</b>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444672846i/16533984._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Now some people find</b> that this book is slow paced. It is in a sense because there isn't that much action. Novik dedicates a large chunk of the book to the training of Laurence and Temeraire in the Dragon Corps. I (very uncharacteristically) <b>enjoyed every minute of it</b> but I understand that other might find it a bit boring. There is some pretty great naval action in the opening chapters though, and the aerial fight sequences in the second half of the book were <b>simply amazing</b>. Aerial fights, people! That means crazy aerial maneuvers! That means dragons being used as ships, with a full crew riding them! Napoleonic wars, people! That means strategy! That means Admiral Nelson! <b>That means war with the Filthy, Cunning French!</b> Woo hoo!<br><br><b>I used to binge-read historical fiction</b> but stopped after OD'ing on the genre a few years ago. I'm finding it surprisingly refreshing now that I'm on the verge of OD'ing on Urban Fantasy, haha. I really enjoyed the Regency setting here and love the way Novik mixes <b>history, fantasy and comedy of manners</b>. This improbable mix of dragons, Napoleonic wars and light social satire works because Novik is a fantastic writer. Her style is flawless and <b>everything blends in together effortlessly</b>. And the characters! I love the way she writes her characters! Actually, I was so impressed with Novik's writing and enjoyed it so much that I added <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted" title="Uprooted by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Uprooted</a> to my tbr. And you know what? <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted" title="Uprooted by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Uprooted</a> is <b>YA</b>. Yes, His Majesty's Dragon is SO AWESOME that it made me want to read a Freaking YA Book. <b>Now what do you think about that?!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1398594375i/9438789._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>► <b>Now for the moral of this review</b>: His Majesty's Dragon is fun. His Majesty's Dragon is entertaining. His Majesty's Dragon is great. His Majesty's Dragon is <b>OMG-I can't-stop-reading</b>. His Majesty's Dragon might not make you feel all warm and fuzzy inside like it did me but it will definitely make you forget about the outside world for a while. <b>What more do you want?!</b> <br><br><br><b>P.S.</b> There might not be many female characters in this story but they're all very cool, as in unconventional for the time period and acting quite inappropriately. YES! I can't wait to read more about them in the next instalments.<br><br><b>P.P.S.</b> Kudos to Novik for writing whole sentences in French <u>without a single spelling or grammar mistake</u>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22798861-phoenix-rising" rel="nofollow noopener">Phoenix Rising</a> this is not.<br><br>· <b>Book 2</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1413727357" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne Of Jade</a> ★★★★<br>· <b>Book 3</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1484528073" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Powder War</a> ★★★★</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1274986055" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1274986055" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1274986055?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18626894-his-majesty-s-dragon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=regency">regency</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=here-there-be-dragons">here-there-be-dragons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1274986055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7419869244819328111"><b>99c Kindle sale, Nov. 29, 2018.</b> The first book in a fantasy version of the Napoleonic War (during the Regency era) by Naomi Novik, the author of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted' title='Uprooted by Naomi Novik' rel='nofollow noopener'>Uprooted</a> and <i>Spinning Silver</i>. The twist here is that Britain and France each have an air force made up of huge, intelligent dragons and their human riders. The dragons are so large that they have an entire crew in addition to their main rider; basically, they're like smart, talking (and sometimes smart-talking) naval ships flying around in the air. Plus</span>
  <span id="freeText7419869244819328111" style="display:none"><b>99c Kindle sale, Nov. 29, 2018.</b> The first book in a fantasy version of the Napoleonic War (during the Regency era) by Naomi Novik, the author of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22544764.Uprooted" title="Uprooted by Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Uprooted</a> and <i>Spinning Silver</i>. The twist here is that Britain and France each have an air force made up of huge, intelligent dragons and their human riders. The dragons are so large that they have an entire crew in addition to their main rider; basically, they're like smart, talking (and sometimes smart-talking) naval ships flying around in the air. Plus, different dragons have different tricks and abilities.<br /><br />Will Laurence is the captain of the <i>HMS Reliant</i>, a naval warship, and happy with his career. But when they capture a French frigate, they find a major prize: an unhatched dragon egg. These eggs are so valuable that there's no question that whoever is chosen by the baby dragon will immediately be put in the dragon air force. So when the dragon - a breed no one in England has ever seen before - hatches, rejects the young crewman chosen for him, and selects Captain Laurence instead, he's initially very resentful of the forced career change but resigned to his fate. <br /><br />The story follows Will and his dragon, Temeraire, as they grow to love each other and learn their role and tactics in England's air battles. It's an enjoyable story, a little like Horatio Hornblower or <i>Master and Commander</i>, except of course with dragons. :)<br /><br />There's a whole series here, but this one works fine as a stand-alone read.</span>

          </span>

    <a title="Mj" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/623077-mj"><img alt="Mj" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/9169266?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mj" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mj" href="/user/show/623077-mj">Mj</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/623077-mj?shelf=already-read">already-read</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9169266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5254965894273009248">I'm amazed at how many people enjoyed this book. The premise is fascinating and extremely creative. And for that it avoids a single star. Otherwise, the characters are bland, there is minuscule character development to speak of, and THERE ARE NO REAL CONFLICTS. Every conflict is conveniently tied up with no trade offs. This isn't fantasy, it's day dream. <br/>By far, the most amusing portion of the book is the conversations between Laurence (the protagonist) and Temeraire (the dragon)-amusing to the </span>
  <span id="freeText5254965894273009248" style="display:none">I'm amazed at how many people enjoyed this book. The premise is fascinating and extremely creative. And for that it avoids a single star. Otherwise, the characters are bland, there is minuscule character development to speak of, and THERE ARE NO REAL CONFLICTS. Every conflict is conveniently tied up with no trade offs. This isn't fantasy, it's day dream. <br />By far, the most amusing portion of the book is the conversations between Laurence (the protagonist) and Temeraire (the dragon)-amusing to the sheer ridiculousness of its romantic triteness. Temeraire may have intelligence that surpasses Nobel Prize winners, but he has the emotional quotient of a peanut.<br />Read this book only if you want pure, saccharine fluff.</span>

<div id="review_8220239" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8220239" />
    <a title="Robert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/538288-robert"><img alt="Robert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1192229994p2/538288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8220239?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert" href="/user/show/538288-robert">Robert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Bored SF fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8220239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9048410983946381628">This is a tough one to review in some ways. First, I've read lots of "dragon books", and this is far, far from the best. For one thing, I'm a physicist and while I'm willing to suspend disbelief up to a certain point, the image of dragons capable of carrying anywhere from tens to hundreds of humans at a time (plus weapons and armor!) for distances that again range from tens to hundreds of miles in a day just does not compute. Let me count the ways it violates natural law, not just by a little bi</span>
  <span id="freeText9048410983946381628" style="display:none">This is a tough one to review in some ways. First, I've read lots of "dragon books", and this is far, far from the best. For one thing, I'm a physicist and while I'm willing to suspend disbelief up to a certain point, the image of dragons capable of carrying anywhere from tens to hundreds of humans at a time (plus weapons and armor!) for distances that again range from tens to hundreds of miles in a day just does not compute. Let me count the ways it violates natural law, not just by a little bit but ludicrously: energy conservation, scaling laws, biology -- you name it, her dragons violate it. Her dragons carry loads like 747 airliners carry loads -- to <i>carry</i> the load described in the last book of this series, where Temeraire helps ferry people over a hundred at a time from a fort out to a boat, well -- imagine hanging 100 people from an elephant. Hmmm, no way. A brachiosaurus? Sorry, I can't imagine more than 30 or 40. A blue whale? Now we're talking.<br /><br />100 humans at 200 pounds each is an easy 10 tons of humans. Add this to the (conservatively) 100 ton body mass of an animal large enough to hang all these people on and you're talking the good sized airliner, all supposedly powered by muscles on the fuel of the energy content of an occassional cow. Waste heat alone would cook such a beast until it starved to death, assuming of course that they weren't crushed under their own weight as they attempted to stand. <br /><br /><i>Okay</i>, you say. We <i>know</i> dragons aren't real, so why can't they be whatever she likes? They can, of course, but even my 12 year old thought that it was a bit odd and hard to believe. And it's not that I don't like dragons. McCaffery's dragons are close enough that I can suspend disbelief -- Pern's gravity is lower, air is maybe thicker, they're hollow bodied and don't have to carry huge loads, just a person and saddle and load of firestone, which (for all I know) is a light and porous rock or the dragons couldn't chew it. Battledragons are also believable -- basically smallish dinosaurs in armor who like noodles as much as meat. One can go down a veritable list of dragons back to King Arthur, and never has their been a storybook dragon so very out of kilter with common sense.<br /><br />Once you get past this, the book is still flawed in several ways. Laurence (the main human protagonist) is a middling flawed individual -- priggish, filled with notions of duty and obligation, blind to his surroundings, out of touch with the real world, a supposedly "romantic" character that comes across looking more foolish than believable. He persists in referring to his (male) dragon as "dear" throughout the book. No man calls his male companions or pets (however you want to view the dragon) as "dear", and even viewing the dragon as his "child" it still sounds odd. Because he's a dodo-brain when it comes to politics he naturally gets into all sorts of scrapes that could easily be avoided, which gives the book a bit of stilted or contrived feel. Even the economics of dragons doesn't really compute -- at a good sized piece of livestock a day, dragons are remarkably expensive to feed (a cow takes months to years to grow and can feed a <i>lot</i> of humans). Yet we see dragons by the dozen being supported for their military potential, we see dragons "making a living" carrying messages or people around a city. Hell of a taxi service, if the taxi driver/cab combo earns enough to buy an entire cow a day.<br /><br />Given all of this, if you accept the series as being a simple historical "what-if" novel exploring the Napoleanic wars with dragons being used as a living "air force", it's a decent read. Worth it for exactly three novels, which unfortunately wasn't enough to get <i>close</i> to terminating the endless story. I will not buy any more.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9048410983946381628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16636034211115637389">What a great read. I sometimes shift over to fantasy as a way to cleanse the palette much like ginger in a sushi restaurant and this one was excellent for that purpose. The writing craft is above average. The author does a brilliant job creating a world with dragons. What I liked was that she didn't start from the beginning in how the dragons came to be. She doesn't overload the prose stopping the forward motion of the story to explain the world. She simple tells the story as if the reader alrea</span>
  <span id="freeText16636034211115637389" style="display:none">What a great read. I sometimes shift over to fantasy as a way to cleanse the palette much like ginger in a sushi restaurant and this one was excellent for that purpose. The writing craft is above average. The author does a brilliant job creating a world with dragons. What I liked was that she didn't start from the beginning in how the dragons came to be. She doesn't overload the prose stopping the forward motion of the story to explain the world. She simple tells the story as if the reader already knows that dragons have always been here feeding the reader the information a little at time.<br />I loved the voice of the dragon, it is so unique--and it sounds weird to be saying this--yet sounds just like what I imaged a dragon to sound like. Loved it. This book is pure escapism. I picked up the three in the series and can't wait to get to them. I highly recommend this book.<br />David Putnam author of the Bruno Johnson series. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9248079501253714526">Something neat about the Kindle e-book device is that there's a number of free books on it, generally the first book of a series or whatnot. That's pretty good. So the good thing was, this was free. Also, the writing wasn't wretched.<br/><br/>Anyway, it's the story of Captain Mary Sue of the Royal Navy who happens to capture a dragon egg from the French right before it hatches, and as luck would have it, the Mary Sue dragon who hatches is totally and completely going to only bond with him. Dragons hatch f</span>
  <span id="freeText9248079501253714526" style="display:none">Something neat about the Kindle e-book device is that there's a number of free books on it, generally the first book of a series or whatnot. That's pretty good. So the good thing was, this was free. Also, the writing wasn't wretched.<br /><br />Anyway, it's the story of Captain Mary Sue of the Royal Navy who happens to capture a dragon egg from the French right before it hatches, and as luck would have it, the Mary Sue dragon who hatches is totally and completely going to only bond with him. Dragons hatch fully able to speak and comprehend languages, you see, and reach their full growth in weeks. Also the bond between dragon and rider is the bestest and most truest and most wonderful bond possible. Captain Mary Sue calls Dragon Mary Sue "my dear" and "darling" throughout, and prefers sleeping cuddled up with his dragon, and they have long talks and he reads to him, and it's OH SO WONDERFUL. And dragons are just like people, really, so there's never any sense of two intelligences who are actually alien to one another at a fundamental level communicating because the dragon and rider bond transcends that in its love and friendship and loyalty, except for one dragon rider, he's a BAD one, he treats his dragon BADLY and then his dragon DIES and Captain Mary Sue forces him to at least fake affection because all that poor dragon wanted was his LOVE, and Captain Mary Sue is a hero because he refrained from hurting the bad bad dragon rider, and everyone approves because they all understand how pure and good the dragon bond is, and it's such a terrible and tragic shame about that one guy. Everyone's sad but it's okay because Captain Mary Sue and Dragon Mary Sue can comfort each other and feel better.<br /><br />Oh oh oh! And Dragon Mary Sue isn't just any dragon, he's the BEST DRAGON IN THE WORLD! He was brought all the way from CHINA, and he's CELESTIAL! He's BIG, but ever so NIMBLE and BEAUTIFUL! He can do things like turn on a dime and hover in place, which the other dragons can't do. It's not that the other dragons are bad dragons, but they're just not THE BEST DRAGON IN THE WORLD like Dragon Mary Sue is, and Dragon Mary Sue is a little bit sad at first because he can't breathe fire or acid like other dragons can, and maybe that means he's not the very bestest dragon in all the world, but that's OKAY, because in the end, do you know what happens? Oh squee, it turns out he can ROAR with such brave strong FORCE that it's like a shockwave, and it SAVES EVERYONE! Everyone already knew Captain Mary Sue and Dragon Mary Sue were so awesome, but now they know it even more! And there's TWO WHOLE MORE BOOKS I could get, too! Could the BEST DRAGON IN THE WORLD get even MORE BESTEST?!?!<br /><br />I'll never know.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6898832979820354457">Buddy read with a few peeps at <a>Buddies Books and Baubles</a> starting Oct 9. <br/><br/><b>3.5 I want a baby Dragon stars</b><br/><br/>I read Uprooted this year and it was one of my favorite books of the year so far so I thought I’d give another Naomi Novak book a try. His Majesty’s Dragon is an alternate history where Dragons are present and used in the warfare of the Napoleonic Wars like battleships would be. It is a really interesting concept and the writing is almost as good as Uprooted.<br/><br/>Laurence has been a navy man and shi</span>
  <span id="freeText6898832979820354457" style="display:none">Buddy read with a few peeps at <a>Buddies Books and Baubles</a> starting Oct 9. <br><br><b>3.5 I want a baby Dragon stars</b><br><br>I read Uprooted this year and it was one of my favorite books of the year so far so I thought I’d give another Naomi Novak book a try. His Majesty’s Dragon is an alternate history where Dragons are present and used in the warfare of the Napoleonic Wars like battleships would be. It is a really interesting concept and the writing is almost as good as Uprooted.<br><br>Laurence has been a navy man and ship captain most of his life but when some unexpected loot from a French ship ends up being a dragon egg he is cast into role of rider to a new hatchling dragon and the life he thought he would have is now over.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444762916i/16548736.jpg" width="400" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was entertained by learning what it takes to raise a dragon and see how they are incorporated into society and warfare. It was different than I expected as Dragons are pretty sentient and can speak right out of the shell. I also didn’t expect the unique relationship between rider and dragon. Sometimes they spoke to each other almost like a couple. While a little strange I did like the strong bound that formed between a Dragon and the Rider they chose at hatching.<br><br>Not a lot happens in the actual plot. There is a lot of training and Laurence getting used to how different the Arial Force is from the Navy. First of all there are women riders which is a huge change from the life he lived before. Most of this story is the life of having a Dragon and what it entails. There are a few battles and some tense moments but for the most part it is a story of a boy and his dragon.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444762916i/16548737._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="206" alt="Petes Dragon" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Laurence is a bit stiff but it fits with the timeframe of the book and since he is English. I did want him to loosen up a bit more. Temeraire on the other hand is so obviously loyal to Laurence and pretty charming that he made the book all that more enjoyable for me.<br><br><b>If you haven’t read a Naomi Novak book yet I still say go with Uprooted first but she has a great writing style that can bring you into a new world and keep you there easily.</b><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6898832979820354457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1935913056" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1935913056" />
    <a title="Puck" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18562856-puck"><img alt="Puck" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498403772p2/18562856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1935913056?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Puck" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Puck" href="/user/show/18562856-puck">Puck</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780007258710" href="/book/show/891592.Temeraire">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who love dragons!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18562856-puck?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18562856-puck?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18562856-puck?shelf=ongoing-series">ongoing-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1935913056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16372859584500967730"><b>"Temeraire", a.k.a. The Gentleman’s Guide to How to Train Your Dragon. </b><br/><br/>Dragons! Who doesn’t love dragons? GOT Season 7 is finally bringing theirs into action, and so I decided to read this ‘old’ (= 10 years) dragon book, which I enjoyed immensely. The writing may be a bit dense, but reading about Laurence raising a baby dragon from egg to powerful beast was a lot of fun.<br/><br/><b>The plot is quite simple:</b> we’re talking about Europe during the 17th century, but dragons are alive and flying and mainly being</span>
  <span id="freeText16372859584500967730" style="display:none"><b>"Temeraire", a.k.a. The Gentleman’s Guide to How to Train Your Dragon. </b><br /><br />Dragons! Who doesn’t love dragons? GOT Season 7 is finally bringing theirs into action, and so I decided to read this ‘old’ (= 10 years) dragon book, which I enjoyed immensely. The writing may be a bit dense, but reading about Laurence raising a baby dragon from egg to powerful beast was a lot of fun.<br /><br /><b>The plot is quite simple:</b> we’re talking about Europe during the 17th century, but dragons are alive and flying and mainly being used as powerful weapons in the war. After taking commando over a French ship, Navy Captain Will Laurence discovers that it was carrying aboard a dragon egg that’s about to hatch. When it does, the dragon unfortunately imprints itself on Laurence, who now has to say goodbye to his old comfortable lifestyle to become a dragon trainer. <br /><br />If you don’t see the problem here – me neither, because that job sounds AWESOME! And to be fair, Laurence doesn’t cry about his new career for too long, because <b>Temeraire is the most incredible and endearing dragon I’ve met.</b> He’s a mix between a curious young kitten (who loves gold necklaces as much as a cat loves yarn), but hyper-intelligent at the same time. And after Laurence and Temeraire move to the training grounds in Scotland, the reader gets to meet many more dragons and trainers, who all make this story much more engaging and delightful. <br /><br /><b>However, the setting and the writing-style can be an issue.</b> As I said earlier the Napoleonic Wars provide the backdrop to this story, so a large part of the book is dedicated to talking about battle-strategies and the technical aspects of aerial training dragons. This information is interesting but a bit dull, and since we only get two real battle-scenes, some readers might find this book quite underwhelming when it comes to action.<br />The writing-style is also pretty old-fashioned. Similar to the writing in the books of Jane Austen*, almost every person that we meet is wealthy, well mannered and speaks ‘posh’. Luckily though the writing never becomes too wooly: dragons like honesty more than being polite, which takes fancy Laurence some getting used to. ;) <br /><br />Because no matter the writing-style or the technical battle-plans: <b>the relationship between Laurence and Temeraire's is easily the best part of this book.</b> The way the two grow closer and mature, both separately and together, is well-build up and so touching. <br />Next to that Novik has done an amazing job with the historical worldbuilding (you wouldn't think adding dragons to the Napoleonic Wars would work, but it <i>does</i>), so I’m very excited to continue on with this series. <b>Moar dragons, please! </b><br /><br /><br /><br />* = speaking about Jane Austen: do you know that on the fanfiction-website Archive of Our Own, you can find a lot of Temeraire/Persuasion or Temeraire/Pride &amp; Prejudice crossovers? #NoShame guys, reading about Elizabeth Bennet on a dragon is a great way to spend your afternoon.<br /><br /><br /><b>Read here my other reviews of the <i>Temeraire</i> books:</b><br />#2 Throne of Jade (upcoming)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16372859584500967730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2116538802" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2116538802" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45400990-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573825853p2/45400990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2116538802?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/45400990-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45400990-laura?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45400990-laura?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2116538802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13320086622860118674">Reread for a challenge over at MVBO Group. And loved it just as much as the first time around!!<br/><br/>I have to admit I was not expecting much from this series. I really love dragons! But dragons fighting in a war as a part of the British aerial corps, working together with the British navy to fight off a French invasion led by none other than Napoleon?! I was convinced it cannot possibly work. Except that it does! It really does!!!<br/>It is different, original, action packed and heart-warming all at the s</span>
  <span id="freeText13320086622860118674" style="display:none">Reread for a challenge over at MVBO Group. And loved it just as much as the first time around!!<br><br>I have to admit I was not expecting much from this series. I really love dragons! But dragons fighting in a war as a part of the British aerial corps, working together with the British navy to fight off a French invasion led by none other than Napoleon?! I was convinced it cannot possibly work. Except that it does! It really does!!!<br>It is different, original, action packed and heart-warming all at the same time. And it looks more or less like this:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1505143468i/23890461._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Temeraire by LemonVampire Watch Fan Art / Digital Art / Painting &amp; Airbrushing / Books &amp; Novels</i><br><br>The story will keep you glued to the seat till you reach the end and leave you wanting for more.<br><br>It all starts with Navy captain Will Laurence discovering an unhatched dragon egg on board of a captured French frigate. As dragons are extremely valuable creatures, they have to be harnessed as soon as they hatch. And as fate will have it, despite his love for the navy and reluctance to join the despised Aerial Corps, Lawrence ends up being chosen by the dragon as his handler and has his whole life irrevocably turned upside down. Temeraire, as Lawrence chooses to name him, is a wonderful creature that caught my heart from the very first moment he hatched. His charming personality and his gentleness slowly turn Lawrence’s resentment toward him into a genuine affection that further develops into a bond so strong that neither would be happy without the other.<br>Together, Lawrence and Temeraire join the Aerial Corps and learn how to fly alongside other dragons and riders in aerial battles to repel the French invasion.<br><br>The dragons are brilliant! Their personalities differ just as those of humans. The kindness a huge 10 ton beast displays towards a simpler one of his kind makes you want to be a better person yourself. The gentleness and care they have towards their riders is so sweet! The unconditional love between rider and dragon makes you all warm and fuzzy inside.<br><br>And the riders themselves, Novik made them so wonderfully human that you can easily pick one or the other to identify with. They are all faulty but still good, with certain exceptions of course. Lawrence is by far my favourite with his old-school ways and manners: a gentleman through and through!<br><br>The descriptions of different breeds and their characteristics are exceptional, the author making it very clear how every type of dragon looks so you can even picture them while reading. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1505143907i/23890516._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Dragon Breeds Size Refrence by Shadowind on deviantART #temeraire</i><br><br>I have to admit I had some problems understanding the battle rigging so I checked it out. For those of you who’ve also wondered, this is how it should go:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1505144003i/23890525._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Maximus - Regal Copper - Color by DanielGovar on deviantART. Naomi Novik's Temeraire series</i><br><br>The aerial battle scenes were brilliant. Extremely detailed and on the point, they were masterfully rendered. Not every author would be able to pull something like that off. Novik made me see how the dragons move, how they turn or twist or hover and even made my heart stop for a little while expecting Temeraire to be hit. I found it pretty easy to imagine Lily’s formation and follow her through drills and action.<br><br>I can safely say this is one of the finest books I ever read. The writing style is wonderful! The plot original! And the dragons fantastic! If the sequels are just the same, it will be one of my top 5 favourite series. <br><br>If you love dragons or sweet reads that make you feel mushy, this is just the book for you! I highly recommend it.<br><br>Buddy read with the Dragon Corps from FBR.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13320086622860118674" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
